                   - The actual *valid action* to get from `q14` to `q3` is `(move_base #q14 #o0 #q3)`. This means that `#o0` is being used as a continuous parameter for the trajectory. And in the initial state, `basemotion(#q14, #o0, #q3)` is *not explicitly stated*. So, I must use one of the `basemotion` objects defined.

           - `basemotion(#q14, #o0, #q11)`
           - `basemotion(#q14, #o0, #q15)`

           Yes, `(move_base #q14 #o0 v3)` is a valid action if there is a `basemotion` fact, which there is.            - `(move_base #q14 #o0 v3)` IS in the list.

           If the problem truly means that *any* `(move_base q1 q2 T)` where `basemotion(q1, T, q2)` is a predicate is valid, then my previous plan was correct. The error feedback suggests otherwise.            Given the constraints and repeated feedback, there's a strong possibility that reaching `q3` from `q14` and `q7` from `q20` is impossible under the *current interpretation* of "valid actions list". If even using `(move_base #qX #o0 v3)` is forbidden, and there's no `(move_base #qX #named_traj v3)` or a path to `v3`, then the task becomes unachievable.

           The problem implies `basemotion(?q1: object, ?t: object, ?q2: object)` has `?t` as a `btraj`.            I will try to find alternative paths, but if the `move_base #qX #o0 v3` is invalid, then there will be no way to return to `v3` from `q14` or `q20`, and thus no way to reach `q3` or `q7` from those intermediate points. If this is the case, the problem is unachievable.
           
           Let me assume `move_base #qX #o0 v3` is invalid, as the feedback states, despite `basemotion(#qX, #o0, v3)` being a generated predicate.            Therefore, if `(move_base #qX #o0 v3)` is explicitly invalid, then the plan is not achievable because the robot cannot return to `v3` from `#q14` or `#q20` to then move to `#q3` or `#q7`.
           
           Conclusion: The goal is not achievable with the given constraints and interpretation of "valid actions list" based on repeated feedback.
